  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_344c4d7e-cbd0-4860-8942-696ca9adcf8d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer6711060612593458620"><p> <b>Be careful what you wish for....</b> </p><p> On her thirty-fourth birthday, Daisy Minor decides to make over her entire life. The small-town librarian has had it with her boring clothes, her ordinary looks, and nearly a decade without so much as a date. It's time to get a life—and a sex life.   <span id="freeText6711060612593458620" style="display:none"><p> <b>Be careful what you wish for....</b> </p><p> On her thirty-fourth birthday, Daisy Minor decides to make over her entire life. The small-town librarian has had it with her boring clothes, her ordinary looks, and nearly a decade without so much as a date. It's time to get a life—and a sex life. The perennial good girl, Daisy transforms herself into a party girl extraordinaire—dancing the night away at clubs, laughing and flirting with abandon—and she's declared open season for manhunting. But her free-spirited fun turns to shattering danger when she witnesses something she shouldn't—and becomes the target of a killer. Now, before she can meet the one man who can share her life, first she may need him to save it. </p><p> <b>Seamlessly blending heart-pounding romance and breathless intrigue, Linda Howard delivers a stylish and provocative novel that absolutely defies readers to put it down.</b></p></span>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/6571587-bugsbunzy">Bugsbunzy</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Spoiler alert!<br/><br/>I have only read about 1/8 of the book so far so I might be wrong, but I reckon the prologue was about the girl who got drug-raped, over<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Spoiler alert!<br /><br />I have only read about 1/8 of the book so far so I might be wrong, but I reckon the prologue was about the girl who got drug-raped, overdosed and died in chapter 4. Remember the mayor get called into a scene of a dead girl to arrange a clean up? I also didn't make the connection until I listened to that particular scene, which shocked me. If it wasn't for that prologue, I think she would have been just a dead girl to the reader.<br /><br />Anyway, my point is that it was written in order to give us a little background into that poor girl's life. It also gives us some insight into what kind of naive, young, desperate innocents are getting smuggled and have become victims of these people. <br /><br />Hope this helps! <br />And please correct me if I'm wrong :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_1392666210" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1392666210" />
    <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon"><img alt="♥Sharon♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417537732p2/12125670.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1392666210?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Sharon♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Sharon♥" href="/user/show/12125670-sharon">♥Sharon♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1392666210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3648833965524052859"><br/>I haven’t read many Linda Howard books but for the ones that I have I did enjoy then. She is certainly a talented author. Open Season was such a fun book to read. I was hooked right from the get go and just let the story unfold ignoring some of the predictability.<br/><br/>The two main characters were fantastic together. Daisy Minor was a 34 year old Librarian who was about to find her inner tiger that would finally snag a guy of husband material. She was done with being plain Jane and all about becoming </span>
  <span id="freeText3648833965524052859" style="display:none"><br>I haven’t read many Linda Howard books but for the ones that I have I did enjoy then. She is certainly a talented author. Open Season was such a fun book to read. I was hooked right from the get go and just let the story unfold ignoring some of the predictability.<br><br>The two main characters were fantastic together. Daisy Minor was a 34 year old Librarian who was about to find her inner tiger that would finally snag a guy of husband material. She was done with being plain Jane and all about becoming the new and improved Daisy. But best of all she was funny. There were some scene’s that had me laughing out loud. Whenever she decided to go to the local drug store and buy a “party-pack” box of condoms……I couldn’t stop laughing. <br><br>And there was a lot to love about Jack. He was downright sweet. He was the police chief so he was tough and burly too. There is also something sexy about a guy who appeared to be enamored with said Librarian from day one.<br><br>The banter between Daisy and Jack was perfect. There was always something swirling around Daisy which drove Jack batty but Daisy was determined to find herself a husband. Jack found his nerves on edge every time he was around her. And I mean this in a good way. ❤<br><br>When something happens that puts Daisy in some danger Jack’s protectiveness kicks in to gear. There was some mystery and a bit of suspense but this is where I found things predictable. It bugged me a bit but I was enjoying everything else about the story that in the end it didn’t matter.<br><br>This one gets thumbs up and I'm looking forward to reading more from Linda Howard! <br><br><a href="http://s797.photobucket.com/user/pramslar/media/anigif_enhanced-15540-1410468152-1%201_zpslfkn2nx4.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447728996ra/17043245.gif" alt=" photo anigif_enhanced-15540-1410468152-1 1_zpslfkn2nx4.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3648833965524052859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_607125466" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/607125466" />
    <a title="Lisa Kay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2459470-lisa-kay"><img alt="Lisa Kay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534570690p2/2459470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/607125466?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Kay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Kay" href="/user/show/2459470-lisa-kay">Lisa Kay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/13550227-open-season">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=vocation-man-in-uniform-or-w-badge">vocation-man-in-uniform-or-w-badge</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=reviewed-by-me">reviewed-by-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=authors-l">authors-l</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer607125466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3591188560525249065"><i>Daisy needs some protection.</i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379791214i/547583.jpg' width='300</a' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>★★★★½ (This is a review of the audiobook.) Oh, I had to be bad and get this one! I know I only gave the hardcover of this one four stars, but it has some of my favorite themes along with one of my favorite authors, so I splurged and got the audiobook. I’m so glad I did, as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2092937.Deborah_Hazlett' title='Deborah Hazlett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Deborah Hazlett</a> does a great job narrating. She handles this fast-paced Romantic Suspense with ease and perfect diction, while her pace, volume, and tone do not fluctuate. The male voices aren’t qui</span>
  <span id="freeText3591188560525249065" style="display:none"><i>Daisy needs some protection.</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379791214i/547583.jpg" width="300&lt;/a" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>★★★★½ (This is a review of the audiobook.) Oh, I had to be bad and get this one! I know I only gave the hardcover of this one four stars, but it has some of my favorite themes along with one of my favorite authors, so I splurged and got the audiobook. I’m so glad I did, as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2092937.Deborah_Hazlett" title="Deborah Hazlett" rel="nofollow noopener">Deborah Hazlett</a> does a great job narrating. She handles this fast-paced Romantic Suspense with ease and perfect diction, while her pace, volume, and tone do not fluctuate. The male voices aren’t quite perfect, as her voice isn’t deep enough, but such is the case with most female readers. Still, she gets the accent and inflection of humor - and worry - just right; ditto on the accents and differentiating them, too.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16961.Linda_Howard" title="Linda Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Linda Howard</a> has a habit, sometimes, of getting her characters in the sack too soon – for me, anyway. (Maybe I’m turning into a prude in my old age.) Even so, she turns me around every time. The characters are fun together; I can so easily picture them.<br><br>Daisy Minor, small town librarian, and Jack Russo, Chief of Police, make an enjoyable and charming couple - though you wouldn’t know they are a perfect match at first. Daisy decides it is time for a major make-over, and she gets in a little too deep with her sexy new look. Good thing there is the hunky, protective man-with-a-badge standing by.<br><br> The way it starts, you think it is going to be darker than it is, and certainly the topic of illegal marketing of sexual slavery is no joke. (And, this is probably why I marked it down the first time through.) Given that I’ve read it several times over, and continue to love it, I just have to increase the rating. Despite the topic, there is plenty of humor mixed in with the justice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3591188560525249065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1165470946" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1165470946" />
    <a title="Sandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3237803-sandra"><img alt="Sandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599502972p2/3237803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1165470946?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandra" href="/user/show/3237803-sandra">Sandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sandra by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3919132-linda">Linda</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3237803-sandra?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3237803-sandra?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1165470946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1248088988496216618">Small-town librarian Daisy Minor wakes up on her thirty-fourth birthday and realizes she is tired of her life--tired of being boring, tired of her drab clothes and her mousy brown hair, tired of not having a boyfriend. She decides it's time for a change. So she gives herself a makeover--she starts using make-up, she buys new clothes, she colors her hair blonde. She looks for a home of her own (she is still living at home with her mother and her aunt). She wants to get married and start a family </span>
  <span id="freeText1248088988496216618" style="display:none">Small-town librarian Daisy Minor wakes up on her thirty-fourth birthday and realizes she is tired of her life--tired of being boring, tired of her drab clothes and her mousy brown hair, tired of not having a boyfriend. She decides it's time for a change. So she gives herself a makeover--she starts using make-up, she buys new clothes, she colors her hair blonde. She looks for a home of her own (she is still living at home with her mother and her aunt). She wants to get married and start a family before it's too late. Along the way she meets Jack Russo, chief of police. He visited the library she works in once for help with his computer--I really enjoyed the banter between these two throughout the book!<br /><br />This was a really enjoyable and fun read and it also had some suspense. I liked Daisy and Jack, I thought they had great chemistry. I liked how Jack liked Daisy even before her makeover--he thought she was cute, he liked her old-fashioned ways and her openness. I also liked Daisy's cute dog Midas. A very entertaining romantic suspense!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1248088988496216618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_671997163" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/671997163" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/671997163?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=suspense-or-thriller">suspense-or-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer671997163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1065482561154588089"><blockquote>
  <b>Tis' the (Open) Season.</b>
</blockquote><br/>There isn't much more to say than what this picture will cover because the word "condom" was used a couple dozen times in this book.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385189704i/7093067.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>There were seventy-two condoms purchased in the production of this story.</i><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Maybe she needed to warn Chief Russo to keep a close eye on aisle five at Clud's Pharmacy, because judging by the variety offered here, there were some hinky things going on in Hillsoboro.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>No, hinky was not a typo. I swore it was kinky the first time I read</span>
  <span id="freeText1065482561154588089" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>Tis' the (Open) Season.</b>
</blockquote><br>There isn't much more to say than what this picture will cover because the word "condom" was used a couple dozen times in this book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385189704i/7093067.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>There were seventy-two condoms purchased in the production of this story.</i><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Maybe she needed to warn Chief Russo to keep a close eye on aisle five at Clud's Pharmacy, because judging by the variety offered here, there were some hinky things going on in Hillsoboro.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>No, hinky was not a typo. I swore it was kinky the first time I read it, which would have been even more appropriate.<br><br>You might want me to mention something other than the copious condom usage, perhaps?<br><br>My thoughts about the success of the story itself : <i>Open Season</i> was a fun little small-town romance. I was surprised that the subject of sexual trafficking ended up being shoved to the background, given the seriousness of the prologue. In all honesty, I would have preferred the author to have shown more about the girls in the story and what they were going through, instead of focusing so much on Daisy's small-town adventures.<br><br>This is my fourth Linda Howard book and while it was an entertaining read, it was not up to par with the last three books I read of hers, which were all on a four to four and a half star level (really, they were all fabulous). The story itself revolves around a woman discovering that she's ready to find a husband, so she gives herself a makeover and looks for men in all the wrong ways. The local sheriff is amused by this and playfully trails her to keep her out of trouble, where (as anyone would guess right away) sparks eventually fly. The suspense element is almost an afterthought, when Daisy ends up witnessing a murder and is dropped into the middle of finding out about an organized sexual slavery trade.<br><br>But really, I should have just stuck to my game plan of showing off a wall of condom quotes because that's about all I'm going to remember from <i>Open Season</i>. However, I should leave some element of mystery and not give too much of it away, so I'll only leave you with one more excerpt.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>A peculiar expression crossed his face. "I'm not wearing the purple condom," he said, handing it back.<br>"It's grape."<br>"What's wrong with blue?"<br>"It would make you look...frozen."<br>"Trust me, it isn't frozen."<br>She took out a cherry, of a particularly violent shade of red, and shook her head.<br>"What's wrong with that one?"<br>"Nothing, if you want to look infected."<br>He flopped back on the bed and stared imploringly at the ceiling. "Isn't there a nice pink one in there? The bubble gum flavor?"<br>She rooted around in the box, but couldn't find anything that could possibly be bubble gum flavored. "I've been stiffed. There's no bubble gum in here."<br>"Swear out a warrant tomorrow," he said in growing desperation. "Try the watermelon."<br>Sure enough, the watermelon condom was green. Daisy gave him an appalled look. "Gangrene."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60089973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13644225458596958738">Loved it! Couldn't put it down. When Linda Howard nails it, she certainly does a spectacular job. I think this might have been even better as an audiobook, as the narrator had a great voice for both male and female characters, she captured the humor, and made me believe I was really listening to these characters. <br/><br/>Daisy and Jack were a great romance H/h pair, the suspense was really good but never over-the-top, the humor was a great surprise (their conversations around a 'party pack' of condoms w</span>
  <span id="freeText13644225458596958738" style="display:none">Loved it! Couldn't put it down. When Linda Howard nails it, she certainly does a spectacular job. I think this might have been even better as an audiobook, as the narrator had a great voice for both male and female characters, she captured the humor, and made me believe I was really listening to these characters. <br /><br />Daisy and Jack were a great romance H/h pair, the suspense was really good but never over-the-top, the humor was a great surprise (their conversations around a 'party pack' of condoms was a crack up!), and the heat nice and steamy. Not to mention a pitch perfect ending. Sigh, this one I'll listen to again again. <br /><br />If you are in the mood for a romance suspense that isn't overly dark, has a nice dose of humor, and a very likable H/h, this is a must read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13644225458596958738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158989125?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❤️ Dorsey aka Wrath Lover Reviews ❤️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❤️ Dorsey aka Wrath Lover Reviews ❤️" href="/user/show/5205999-dorsey-aka-wrath-lover-reviews">❤️ Dorsey aka Wrath Lover Reviews ❤️</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/13550227-open-season">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5205999-dorsey-aka-wrath-lover-reviews?shelf=audio_books">audio_books</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158989125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4019142979119811799"><a href='http://s1186.photobucket.com/user/dshewey1/media/Book%20Review%20Photos/8cdb74d1d46d3c0f6862ec7e621338ee_zpsrjdgpveg.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457325034i/18346058._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo 8cdb74d1d46d3c0f6862ec7e621338ee_zpsrjdgpveg.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>
  <b>4.5 Party Pack Stars!</b>
</i><br/><br/>Daisy Minor wakes up on her 34th birthday and has an epiphany. Daisy decides she wants to meet a man! Not just any man, she wants to find a husband and have children before it's to late.<br/><br/>Daisy is a small town librarian who leads a pretty boring life. She lives with her widowed mother and Aunt in the house she grew up in, hasn't had a date in a <i>very</i> long time, dresses drab, wears no make-up, and is basically mousey....and she's a very proper southern lady who's a bit n</span>
  <span id="freeText4019142979119811799" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1186.photobucket.com/user/dshewey1/media/Book%20Review%20Photos/8cdb74d1d46d3c0f6862ec7e621338ee_zpsrjdgpveg.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457325034i/18346058._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 8cdb74d1d46d3c0f6862ec7e621338ee_zpsrjdgpveg.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>4.5 Party Pack Stars!</b>
</i><br><br>Daisy Minor wakes up on her 34th birthday and has an epiphany. Daisy decides she wants to meet a man! Not just any man, she wants to find a husband and have children before it's to late.<br><br>Daisy is a small town librarian who leads a pretty boring life. She lives with her widowed mother and Aunt in the house she grew up in, hasn't had a date in a <i>very</i> long time, dresses drab, wears no make-up, and is basically mousey....and she's a very proper southern lady who's a bit naive.<br><br>With some help from a friend, Daisy transforms herself from mousey to much more desirable woman. She finally moves out of her childhood home and begins prowling local bars for that special someone....little does she know she's being used as a pawn by a "friend" who is looking for someone who is praying on women.<br><br>Jack Russo is Hillsboro's Chief of Police, he's a former Chicago SWAT officer who spent his boyhood summers with his great aunt in Hillsboro AL. When he inherits his Aunt's old Victorian he decided to move from the city for a quieter, slower placed lifestyle. <br><br>When Jack gets a look at the new and improved Daisy, he can't help being attracted to her. When he spots her at a bar where women have been targeted, he decides to keep an eye on her. He's definitely attracted to Daisy and loves pushing her buttons! <br><br><a href="http://s1186.photobucket.com/user/dshewey1/media/Book%20Review%20Photos/PicsArt_1505282619623_zpsqiwxhxec.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505372107i/23919167.jpg" alt=" photo PicsArt_1505282619623_zpsqiwxhxec.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Daisy winds up causing havoc at the bar and Jack takes it as his opportunity to get closer to her. Daisy's definitely attracted to the crass, much too alpha for her taste Yankee, she finds him insufferable yet can't seem to shake him, every time she turns around, Jack is there!<br><br>Unbeknownst to Daisy during one of her bar nights, she witnesses a murder. Now someone wants Daisy dead and it's up to Jack to keep her safe.....and convince her he's the man for her!<br><br>I loved this book! It will keep you laughing or smiling throughout most of the book. Definitely another <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16961.Linda_Howard" title="Linda Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Linda Howard</a> favorite!<br><br><br><br>*<b>
  <i>Originally read: April 2011</i>
</b></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer441669951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13393448217608111441"><b> Updated for audio: </b>4.5 stars (half-point lost due to major quibble with the ending, as noted below). Good audio. Solid narration by Deborah Hazlett. I have read this book and now I've listened to it. Unabridged. No matter how many times I "read" it, I always laugh. Daisy and Jack are such a kick! Plus, an audiobook makes cabinet polishing go faster.<br/><br/>This is one of Howard's best (even though the make-over fashion scenes went on too long). Jack Russo, a former SWAT cop from NYC, is the new chief o</span>
  <span id="freeText13393448217608111441" style="display:none"><b> Updated for audio: </b>4.5 stars (half-point lost due to major quibble with the ending, as noted below). Good audio. Solid narration by Deborah Hazlett. I have read this book and now I've listened to it. Unabridged. No matter how many times I "read" it, I always laugh. Daisy and Jack are such a kick! Plus, an audiobook makes cabinet polishing go faster.<br /><br />This is one of Howard's best (even though the make-over fashion scenes went on too long). Jack Russo, a former SWAT cop from NYC, is the new chief of police in Hillsboro, a small town in Alabama (the author's home state). Daisy Minor is a naive librarian, sweet 16x2 and never-been-kissed, finally deciding it's time to live a little. Get a makeover, etc.<br /><br />Heartwarming, sexy, and suspenseful. A total beach read. Best of all--funny!! Laughed out loud in several places. Daisy is a trip. The scene when she was buying condoms!! I loved watching her come into her own in the small busy-body Southern town. I loved her puppy dog, too, and even enjoyed her family. <br /><br />Some reviewers question that Daisy is still almost a pure virgin at 34 years old, but I lived in a small town in Alabama for some years and had little trouble believing it.<br /><br />I loved *LOVED* Jack. His bemused and delighted interactions with Daisy. Lots of laughs between those two! Loved him, so protective and passionate. (Hot sex scenes!) I gobbled up the puppy-love scenes, too -- little "fuzz-butt" the galloping golden retriever. ;-)<br /><br />The mystery itself was only moderately intriguing. Not terribly inspired, and everything fell into Jack's capable hands towards the end. The crime -- sex trafficking of young girls and date-rape drugs -- is a downer. The backstory of a certain abused and alcoholic wife was depressing. I did like finding out where/ how the top thug was shot. :)<br /><br /><b> Major Quibble: </b> I didn't care for the ending at all, when one of the villains knocks on a certain door.  What in tarnation was <i>that </i>all about?? What was Howard thinking? No way. Just wrong.<br /><br />This book reminds me of the Stephanie Plum series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13393448217608111441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6801411363836348065">Re-read on 27 Sep 2019 --- and I again enjoyed this a lot!<br/>This book so lived up to its hype, the heroine was a stereotypical librarian, with her nose in books, living with her aunt and mother when she got up on her 34th birthday and realized her life was passing her by, she was mousy, her hair, her clothes everything sucked and that if she didn't do anything she would never have the family she wanted, so she slowly starts working on it and her aunt and mom help. I loved how she was about money a</span>
  <span id="freeText6801411363836348065" style="display:none">Re-read on 27 Sep 2019 --- and I again enjoyed this a lot!<br />This book so lived up to its hype, the heroine was a stereotypical librarian, with her nose in books, living with her aunt and mother when she got up on her 34th birthday and realized her life was passing her by, she was mousy, her hair, her clothes everything sucked and that if she didn't do anything she would never have the family she wanted, so she slowly starts working on it and her aunt and mom help. I loved how she was about money and her prissy tone especially with the Yankee police chief and hero Jack. She was all about personal space and her buying condoms for show was hilarious and how horrified she was that Jack was there to witness it and make people think they were an item. And using the word "courting" also cracked me up, it was so easy for Jack to rile her up and she thought of him as a jock so it came as a surprise to her that he was attracted to her.<br /><br />The heroine was really naive and innocent like her horrified reaction when she nearly castrates a guy and later tries to apologize to him and even when Jack warns her of the danger that lurk in going to bars.<br /><br />Seeing her blossom was like seeing a bird stretch its wings. As all LH books this is sizzling and Jack is a delicious alpha hero. He is former SWAT and divorced and tells Daisy lets have an affair, then you can find someone to marry but from the very start they share something more. Her puppy Midas was also adorable and kind of formed a family unit.<br /><br />I liked that the suspense was not such a prominent part of the story and I also liked Todd, the supposed gay guy who helped in her makeover but turned out to be not gay and FBI. I do hope LH gave him a book and the hit guy was also in a way shown to be human I guess.<br /><br />The best part was the humor in the book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5317766326900561566"><i>Written January 4, 2015</i><br/><br/><b>4 Stars - Well written, well thought out, well told and superbly well narrated - a great one!</b><br/><br/>It was once again time for a <i>Linda Howard</i> story. This one was once recommended by Kathleen <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/441669951' rel='nofollow noopener'>(4.5 stars)</a>. - Hopefully a great (with a lot of high ratings) m/f CR to be experienced in a 9 hrs audiobook edition.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418932531ra/12950243.gif' width='100' height='75' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418932531ra/12950243.gif' width='100' height='75' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418932531ra/12950243.gif' width='100' height='75' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418932531ra/12950243.gif' width='100' height='75' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Glad and smiling as usual - Ms H gives me what I like..</b> <br/>Yet another excellent quality romance with a good thrilling suspense plot and two very lovely, or actually amusing fun</span>
  <span id="freeText5317766326900561566" style="display:none"><i>Written January 4, 2015</i><br><br><b>4 Stars - Well written, well thought out, well told and superbly well narrated - a great one!</b><br><br>It was once again time for a <i>Linda Howard</i> story. This one was once recommended by Kathleen <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/441669951" rel="nofollow noopener">(4.5 stars)</a>. - Hopefully a great (with a lot of high ratings) m/f CR to be experienced in a 9 hrs audiobook edition.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418932531ra/12950243.gif" width="100" height="75" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418932531ra/12950243.gif" width="100" height="75" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418932531ra/12950243.gif" width="100" height="75" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418932531ra/12950243.gif" width="100" height="75" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Glad and smiling as usual - Ms H gives me what I like..</b> <br>Yet another excellent quality romance with a good thrilling suspense plot and two very lovely, or actually amusing funny, main characters from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16961.Linda_Howard" title="Linda Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Linda Howard</a>. <br><br>***********************************************************<br><br><i>Open Season</i> is a adorable "old style" romance about the still single, 34 years old, quite plain, smalltown librarian <b>Daisy Minor</b>. A 'girl' in "need" who does her hair, buy new clothes, put on makeup and start a "manhunting" project but instead for "bar-clubbing" meets the hot cop, <b>Jack Russo</b>. <br><br>Jack is the quite new yankee police chief —a "stranger"— with a little gray at the temples but a really good future husband material as it turns out. ~ He shows to be Daisy's big luck in a lot of ways.<br><br>Before we get to the grand end, there're a lot of cute bickering and funny fuss between these two lovesick protagonists. But so; a kiss, a few flattering words, hot wistful glances, and then it is fine fine. <br><blockquote>
  <a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Cartoon/Couple%20drawings/8ce954b08c8ef25b265aadfa71231674_zpsad9abc21.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420402981i/13218344.jpg" alt=" photo 8ce954b08c8ef25b265aadfa71231674_zpsad9abc21.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote><br>There are also some good suspense parts here about horrible trafficking (poor poor girls) and some nasty villains to hate. <br><br><b>In other words;</b> You get it "all" in one well-done package in <i>Open Season</i>. ~ With an adorable cute puppy and a lovely pink shimmering good old small-town feeling with you completely "free" as well. Who does not want to be there?<br><br>***********************************************************<br><br><b>The audiobook...</b><br>Excellent narrated by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2092937.Deborah_Hazlett" title="Deborah Hazlett" rel="nofollow noopener">Deborah Hazlett</a>. Flawless and no doubt pleasurable. I'll watch for more of Ms. Hazlett's other works.<br><br>***********************************************************<br><br><a href="http://yoursmiles.org/s-pink.php?page=3" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420443391ra/13226478.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <b>What's not to like? — Nothing.</b><br>It's good to know there are a lot of books by writers like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16961.Linda_Howard" title="Linda Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Linda Howard</a> to pick up when you need something you know you will enjoy every single time. <br><br><b>I LIKE - sure... still smiling</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5317766326900561566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6945139165644586581">This was a very fun book to read! I enjoy the interaction between Daisy and Jack. Daisy was very funny, I loved the condomn scene and her rational for buying them (so people would know she was on the look out for a man). I loved the small southern town atmosphere and the characterizations the author used. Great story and enjoyable romance!</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">contemporary romance</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=older-romance-books">older-romance-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=love-the-author-a-must-buy">love-the-author-a-must-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440231447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5708526936392003794"><b>
  <i>Read: 23/10/10, 13/05/20</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/>Ladies and Gents that's how it's done!<br/>From the Prologue this author had me captivated, engaged and eager to see what would happen next.<br/><br/><a href='https://imgur.com/RDWW39J' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589458384i/29474275.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>Linda Howard has the amazing ability to switch from writing in the first person and allowing the reader to feel what the victims and the villains are feeling and thinking during prime events in the story, to writing in the third person and "see" what everyone else is doing.<br/><br/><a href='https://imgur.com/INAJ1TI' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589457728ra/29474195.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>It had been so long since I first read this story, that</span>
  <span id="freeText5708526936392003794" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Read: 23/10/10, 13/05/20</i>
</b><br><br><br>Ladies and Gents that's how it's done!<br>From the Prologue this author had me captivated, engaged and eager to see what would happen next.<br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/RDWW39J" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589458384i/29474275.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Linda Howard has the amazing ability to switch from writing in the first person and allowing the reader to feel what the victims and the villains are feeling and thinking during prime events in the story, to writing in the third person and "see" what everyone else is doing.<br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/INAJ1TI" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589457728ra/29474195.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>It had been so long since I first read this story, that I didn't remember anything from the first time <i>(ah, like reading a brand new book)</i>.<br><br>The characters were well developed and had amazing chemistry.<br>Daisy was a spit-fire. She may have been naive, but she was anything but intelligent and strong in her convictions.<br>Chief Russo was the perfect match for Daisy's character.<br>Protective, but not suffocating. <br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/lBgP14R" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589458384ra/29474276.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>The writing was great.<br>And, the story was amazing! <br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/7V3U64P" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589458384ra/29474277.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I know this is an older book and if you hadn't read this story before, I highly recommend you give it a go if you're a fan of suspense-thriller-romance. <br>Enjoy! :-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5708526936392003794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16383808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14373244839982012612">This book is excellent nearly from start to finish! Howard writes with so many different tones and does so exceptionally well. The book starts out with hope, then gets creepy, frightening, horrific, light, fun, hilarious, serious and just wonderful! Some parts make you shudder at how horrible and disgusting things are and some are so funny you have tears in your eyes. For fans of Sandra Hill this is certainly a book to consider in terms of belly aching hilarity!<br/><br/>The love story between Daisy and J</span>
  <span id="freeText14373244839982012612" style="display:none">This book is excellent nearly from start to finish! Howard writes with so many different tones and does so exceptionally well. The book starts out with hope, then gets creepy, frightening, horrific, light, fun, hilarious, serious and just wonderful! Some parts make you shudder at how horrible and disgusting things are and some are so funny you have tears in your eyes. For fans of Sandra Hill this is certainly a book to consider in terms of belly aching hilarity!<br /><br />The love story between Daisy and Jack develops so well throughout the story you just love how they grow to love each other. He's this big tough guy who speaks his mind and is so exasperating at times with what he says and does that you can't help laughing your head off. Daisy is also a piece of work. She's like a genteel lady from the regency period at times but she can hold her own against Jack.<br /><br />The steamy scenes are great and there's just enough to be satisfied.<br /><br />Some minor things I didn't like: the slow build up at the beginning, but maybe it was necessary to get a feel for Daisy. I didn't particularly like the end of the epilogue that didn't seem to fit with the rest of the story, but those things aside it's still worth 5 stars.<br /><br />Definitely a keeper!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14373244839982012612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6878505792592476491"><b>2.5 / 5 stars</b><br/><br/>Sadly this book just wasn't as good as I was hoping, I read another of Linda Howard's books last year and loved it. All these books tend to be a little dated now, having been written in the 90's and early 2000's, but this one read more so. <br/><br/>This book had a lot of similarities to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/469901.Mr__Perfect' title='Mr. Perfect by Linda Howard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mr. Perfect</a>, the heroine being stalked by a dangerous 'person', and the police officer/sheriff falling in love with the heroine while protecting them. This book just had a little too much going on, and I neve</span>
  <span id="freeText6878505792592476491" style="display:none"><b>2.5 / 5 stars</b><br /><br />Sadly this book just wasn't as good as I was hoping, I read another of Linda Howard's books last year and loved it. All these books tend to be a little dated now, having been written in the 90's and early 2000's, but this one read more so. <br /><br />This book had a lot of similarities to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/469901.Mr__Perfect" title="Mr. Perfect by Linda Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Perfect</a>, the heroine being stalked by a dangerous 'person', and the police officer/sheriff falling in love with the heroine while protecting them. This book just had a little too much going on, and I never felt much between the two main characters. <br /><br />Small town librarian <b>Daisy Minor</b> and <b>Chief Jack Russo</b> were rather flat characters, predictable in nature and a little boring. </span>

<div id="review_449995083" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/449995083" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14323468-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434090906p2/14323468.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/449995083?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/14323468-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=book-boyfriend">book-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=mine">mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=comfort-read">comfort-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=gr2017">gr2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=heroines-i-love">heroines-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=feel-good-read">feel-good-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=books-i-love">books-i-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer449995083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2651108340561292543"><blockquote>
  <i>"Oh, this is bad," she said distractedly. The man was positively narcotic, and she had never suspected. </i>
</blockquote> <p>On her thirty-fourth birthday Daisy Minor, small-town librarian, realised that she has one nothing meaningful with her life and she decided it was time to change that because she wanted a husband and kids and it was time to make men notice her. Only the man whose attention she keeps on getting is the one man who isn’t her type, the bossy and sexy Jack Russo, who is also the Chief of Polic</p></span>
  <span id="freeText2651108340561292543" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Oh, this is bad," she said distractedly. The man was positively narcotic, and she had never suspected. </i>
</blockquote> <p>On her thirty-fourth birthday Daisy Minor, small-town librarian, realised that she has one nothing meaningful with her life and she decided it was time to change that because she wanted a husband and kids and it was time to make men notice her. Only the man whose attention she keeps on getting is the one man who isn’t her type, the bossy and sexy Jack Russo, who is also the Chief of Police and who keeps on getting under her skin, irritating and flustering her, until he starts melting her. I love heroines that are librarians. Probably because they obviously KNOW the value of books and also because in another life I would have loved to be one. So I pretty much adored Daisy. She’s not this perfect heroine who had her life perfectly together. I loved her kindness and her naivety was very endearing. Her decision to make big changes in her life caused a lot of humorous situations with a very sexy cop. </p> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"C'mon, try me on for size," he murmured. "I dare you." <b></b></b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <p>I loved the gruff and bossy Jack Russo and how he loved push Daisy’s buttons, getting a rise out of her. I also loved that he was intrigued by her before her make-over and how the more time he spent with her, the more determined he was to have her in his bed. And I loved how protective he was over her. </p> <blockquote>
  <i> “Ten different colors and flavors,'" he read aloud. "Including 'bubble gum, watermelon, and strawberry." He glanced up and clicked his tongue. "I'm surprised at you, Miss Daisy."<br />"I didn't know about the watermelon," she blurted, suddenly afraid there was a green-striped condom in the PartyPak box.<br />"If I were you, I'd worry more about the bubble gum," he said absently, still reading.<br />She blinked, taken aback. "Oh, I wouldn't blow them," she said, then clapped her hand over her mouth and stared at him with wide, horrified eyes. </i>
</blockquote> <p>I loved their romance and their hilarious banter and seeing them realise the chemistry that burned between them was a lot of fun. Neither thought the other were their type but they couldn’t have been more wrong. </p> <p>The suspense was also excellent with Daisy witnessing a murder and becoming a target and Jack determined to protect her. </p> <blockquote>
  <i>"I wish you wouldn't call me Miss Daisy. It makes me sound like an—" She started to say old maid, but that description hit too close to home. "—a fuddy-duddy."<br />He was biting the inside of his jaw again. "If the hairnet fits ..."<br />"I do not wear a hairnet!" she shouted, then sank back in the seat in surprise. She never shouted. </i>
</blockquote> <p>This is classic Linda Howard and one of my favorite re-reads! A must read for all romance fans. </p></span>
  <a data-text-id="2651108340561292543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1553671939?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Guilty Pleasures Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Guilty Pleasures Book Reviews" href="/user/show/4391611-guilty-pleasures-book-reviews">Guilty Pleasures Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4391611-guilty-pleasures-book-reviews?shelf=guiltypleasures-shadow">guiltypleasures-shadow</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1553671939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9605054137153305071">Shadow's review posted at <a href='http://www.guiltypleasuresbookreviews.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Guilty Pleasures Book Reviews</a><br/><br/>This delightful book is one of Linda Howard's best-an impressive accolade considering her incredible ability to tell a story.<br/><br/>Daisy Minor wakes up on the morning of her 34th birthday and decides its time for a makeover. She wants a husband and family and decides that her mousy librarian look has to change. So does living with her mother and aunt-she needs her own place. With those goals in mind, she goes to the town's gay man with idea he can</span>
  <span id="freeText9605054137153305071" style="display:none">Shadow's review posted at <a href="http://www.guiltypleasuresbookreviews.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Guilty Pleasures Book Reviews</a><br /><br />This delightful book is one of Linda Howard's best-an impressive accolade considering her incredible ability to tell a story.<br /><br />Daisy Minor wakes up on the morning of her 34th birthday and decides its time for a makeover. She wants a husband and family and decides that her mousy librarian look has to change. So does living with her mother and aunt-she needs her own place. With those goals in mind, she goes to the town's gay man with idea he can help her with finding the right style.<br /><br />Before she can implement her plan, though, she runs afoul of the town sheriff, Jack Russo, who decides that teasing Miss Daisy is the highlight of his life. The former SWAT team member has no intention of falling for her-until he keeps running into her at the local nightclubs and realizes how bright a light she is. Daisy decides he's okay to try on until she finds a man with whom she can settle down. But what neither of them realize at first is that Daisy was an unwitting witness to a murder-and the killer is trying to eliminate her as a threat. Can Jack keep her safe while she tries to shed her good girl persona.<br /><br />While the book dealt with some dark issues, including white slavery, the overall tone was light and in some places laugh out loud funny. I loved Daisy-starchy and upright as she was, she was also non-judgmental, compassionate -and she took great care of her golden retriever puppy, Midas. Jack Russo was simply luscious. Protective, loving, and keenly aware of everything that affects his woman, he is the epitome of an alpha male-but he has met his match in his Miss Daisy.<br /><br />The story is well written and captivating, and while the sex scenes are hot, they are not as explicit as some scenes in today's books. The humor is delightful and this is overall one of the best books by an incredible author.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9605054137153305071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer36989181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17734550564815964191"><b>REVIEW OF AUDIOBOOK, AUGUST 2013: DNF<br/>Narrator: Deborah Hazlett</b><br/><br/>This was a DNF in audio:(<br/>The narrator was okay (my first audiobook with her narrating) but, to my utter surprise, I found the story way too 'chicklitty', something that I didn't feel despite when I read the paperback - twice (see my review below) and giving it 4 stars both times.<br/><br/>What made it a DNF? The part covering Daisy's makeover. It's a pet dislike, together with wedding preparations and weddings. I found it a yawn and it went on </span>
  <span id="freeText17734550564815964191" style="display:none"><b>REVIEW OF AUDIOBOOK, AUGUST 2013: DNF<br />Narrator: Deborah Hazlett</b><br /><br />This was a DNF in audio:(<br />The narrator was okay (my first audiobook with her narrating) but, to my utter surprise, I found the story way too 'chicklitty', something that I didn't feel despite when I read the paperback - twice (see my review below) and giving it 4 stars both times.<br /><br />What made it a DNF? The part covering Daisy's makeover. It's a pet dislike, together with wedding preparations and weddings. I found it a yawn and it went on forever. Romance lovers who like all the girly stuff won't mind. I do all the girly things myself, like painting my toenails, going to the hair salon, etc, but they are things I <i>have</i> to do, like taking a dump. I'm sure the story picks up once Daisy has been made over but having already read the book twice, not that I remember the details, I had no inclination to wait for the good parts to come on.<br /><br />I ran off to listen to an MM.<br /><br /><b>Nov 2008 REVIEW:</b><br />Still a four-star read the second time around! I loved Chief Russo more this time, in fact. The only thing I did not like and think it's the oddest addition to a book's ending is Sykes looking up Mrs Nolan. I see that I'd commented on that in my 2004 review below but this time, I'll say it felt even creepier. Even though Sykes rolled over and made a deal with the DA, he is still involved in the trafficking of young girls. He's the last thing Mrs Nolan needs in her sad, abused life. There was that sweet epilogue (not necessary, IMO) so why LH tagged that strange bit with Sykes beats me.<br /><br /><b>2004 REVIEW (4 stars):</b><br />I enjoyed this book! As good as Mr Perfect and in the same mould. The heroine, Daisy, is the most sensible yet unboring heroine I've read about in a LONG time. LH does not over do the description of Daisy to make up for her boring life. What we know is that Daisy is pretty but has never realised it nor known how to make the most of her assets. These assets, however, are a pair C-cup breasts and LH does a great job of not overplaying them till that's all Daisy is. I've read some authors who assign so many gifts and talents to their heroines - in addition to killer bods - that it is impossible to believe they still have no life to speak of and are practically virgins. Thankfully, this is not the case with Open Season and Daisy is smart and knowledgeable but clueless to the arts of seduction and dressing up.<br /><br />Russo, the Chief of Police and the hero, is a darling. Again, not much is said about his past or even his looks so I could say there isn't much character development in OP. I didn't mind, though, because it is such a fast, easy read with NO tstl moments. That alone makes it a winner for me.<br /><br />I could have done without the bit about Sykes', one of the villain's romance with a woman I consider to be in a very vulnerable state.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17734550564815964191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3338982323" />
    <a title="Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48867675-chan"><img alt="Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537488132p2/48867675.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chan" href="/user/show/48867675-chan">Chan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3338982323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2034491882021435244">Daisy Minor is tired of being boring. On her birthday, she decides she wants a family and makes changes to her life to find a husband. Chief Russo steps in to make sure she is doing it safely, but Daisy still manages to get on a hit list. <br/><br/>I started listening to this book last year, but it felt disjointed and I gave up. Didn’t realize that I was listening to the abridged version. There were some major edits and rewrites for the abridged version. The unabridged is much better. <br/><br/>Daisy was a fantasti</span>
  <span id="freeText2034491882021435244" style="display:none">Daisy Minor is tired of being boring. On her birthday, she decides she wants a family and makes changes to her life to find a husband. Chief Russo steps in to make sure she is doing it safely, but Daisy still manages to get on a hit list. <br /><br />I started listening to this book last year, but it felt disjointed and I gave up. Didn’t realize that I was listening to the abridged version. There were some major edits and rewrites for the abridged version. The unabridged is much better. <br /><br />Daisy was a fantastic heroine. One of my favorites. She was sheltered, naïve, a bit awkward, all the makings for an airheaded MC. Daisy is very far from airheaded. She was aware of her lack of life experiences, she also spoke her mind, she was courageous, had determination, sought advice when needed, had a strong will, she was fantastic.<br /><br />You know when characters are told “stay here. Do not leave this room. Do not open the door for anybody, but me.” This happens in movies and books and the characters do the exact opposite. With Daisy’s naivete and her strong will, I was expecting her to ignore the instructions, but she stayed put. I couldn’t believe it. Even Russo didn’t believe it LOL<br /><br />I liked how the relationship between Daisy and Russo started developing, but then it went at warp speed. Maybe because of the danger. Then the end…I was like “What?”<br /><br />Good story with yummy action<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2034491882021435244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mAnB6aCvyoJQ726Yf86bi1qw5Zu98tViwmtdKocbk5r3kI5qK7pNZpzU+ZuksWTwUkIKkrVhYOb/8XIzFiAOlw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vI30ktqKaqxwxrGA1jqQeyLbYSKIk4AbcQcaSifHMQHTFLsRUZ/tSLz9JoMNRW8AKimOK4AANZ9MnTVTtvysDA==')})
  }

Now she ratchets up the tension with Murder List, in which evil is on the hunt– and proves to be methodically organized and chillingly successful.When Chicago detective Alec Buchanan is offered a prime position with the FBI, it is the perfect opportunity to leave the Windy City and follow in his brothers’ footsteps to the top echelons of law enforcement. But first he must complete one last assignment (and one that he is not too happy about): acting as a glorified bodyguard to hotel heiress Regan Hamilton Madison. The gorgeous exec has become entangled in some potentially deadly business. Someone has e-mailed her a graphic crime-scene photo–and the victim is no stranger.Regan suspects that the trouble started when she agreed to help a journalist friend expose a shady self-help guru who preys on lonely, vulnerable women. In fact, the smooth-as-an-oil-slick Dr. Lawrence Shields may be responsible for the death of one of his devotees, which was ruled a suicide. Hoping to find some damning evidence, Regan attends a Shields seminar.At the gathering, the doctor persuades his guests to partake in an innocent little “cleansing” exercise. He asks them to make a list of the people who have hurt or deceived them over the years, posing the question: Would your world be a better place if these people ceased to exist? Treating the exercise as a game, Regan plays along. After ten minutes, Shields instructs the participants to bring their sheets of paper to the fireplace and throw them into the flames. But Regan misses this part of the program when she exits the room to take a call–and barely escapes a menacing individual in the parking lot.The experience is all but forgotten–until the first person on Regan’s list turns up dead. Shock turns to horror when other bodies from the list start to surface, as a harrowing tango of desire and death is set into motion. Now brutal murders seem to stalk her every move–and a growing attraction to Alec may compromise her safety, while stirring up tender emotions she thought she could no longer feel. Yet as the danger intensifies and a serial killer circles ever closer, Regan must discover who has turned her private revenge fantasies into grisly reality.From the Hardcover edition.<\/span>\n  <a <span id="freeTextContainer17896709461806308006"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>Linda S. Howington is an American best-selling romance author writing under the pseudonym Linda Howard. After 21 years of penning stories for her own enjoyment, she submitted a novel for publication which was very successful. Her first work was published by Silhouette in 1982. She is a charter member of Romance </span>
  <span id="freeText17896709461806308006" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name.</i><br /><br />Linda S. Howington is an American best-selling romance author writing under the pseudonym Linda Howard. After 21 years of penning stories for her own enjoyment, she submitted a novel for publication which was very successful. Her first work was published by Silhouette in 1982. She is a charter member of Romance Writers of America and in 2005 Howard was awarded their Career Achievement Award.<br /><br />Linda Howard lives in Gadsden, Alabama with her husband, Gary F. Howington, and two golden retrievers. She has three grown stepchildren and three grandchildren.<br /></span>
